field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item"> This lesson will teach students that there is no conflict between scientific findings and belief in God. It will do so by explaining that God is not a being in the universe, but is Being itself. The students will also understand the different types of questions science and religion answer. <br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1. Students will be able to explain that calling God Creator means that God is Being itself and is not a being within the universe.  </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. Students will be able to define the Big Bang Theory and discuss Catholicism’s role in its discovery.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. Students will be able to explain how to interpret Genesis correctly (i.e., as mythical poetry) and the power of myth in conveying truth.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. Students will be able to state the differences between the goals and methods of science and those of theology.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Construct an effective logical argument in order to disprove the assumption that science and theology are in a state of conflict using examples from this lesson.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Integrate their Catholic faith with other academic disciplines. </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Distinguish terms that alleviate apparent contradictions between faith and science. </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Demonstrate an awareness of the differences between philosophical and scientific modes of thinking.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="5"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Demonstrate how Catholics have traditionally understood God.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Interpret and understand the truth of myths. </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Previous Assigned Homework: </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.chrisrossarthur.com/uploads/3/8/5/9/38596187/pandoras_box.pdf"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Pandora’s Box</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> or any other myths the teacher wants to assign.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/5d3b1fbf6cb5ab00017659d8/t/5efcf0eb44346d54c7c83da8/1593635051315/The+Parable+of+the+Prodigal+Son.pdf"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Prodigal Son </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>or any other parable in the New Testament that the teacher wants to assign. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class time: 75 Minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li>Pedagogy </li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A.) Bellringer: Have students find artistic Representations of God to show misconceptions of who God is.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>B.) Engage in a metaphysical discussion of God’s nature ending in discussion of God’s role as Creator.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>C.) Discussion of what is the Big Bang Theory.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>D.) Show video from National Geographic and provide a summarized explanation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>E.) Discussion of apparent conflict/contradictions using the thermometer game to engage students.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>F.) Discussion of what Genesis is and incorporate discussion on myth.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>G.) Defining the methodology of theology and science: 2 approaches to reality.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>H.) Show video about Georges Lemaitre and discuss its implications.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I.) Exit Ticket: Do scientific findings (ex. Evolution, Big Bang Theory) disprove God or make it harder to believe in God.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Our assessment will be a choice board assignment. </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.edutopia.org/article/using-choice-boards-boost-student-engagement"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(See link for info about choice boards</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>). The choice board will take place within our unit on the Introduction to Catholicism’s larger framework. They will have to choose one assignment that corresponds to the difficulty category and have to choose one assignment that corresponds to the lesson column. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <table> <tbody> <tr> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lessons within the Unit</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Easy</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Moderate</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Hard</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> </tr> <tr> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Faith and Science Lesson</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The students will take a 20 point quiz, which will be a simple recollection/recall of the lesson. Ex. “True or False:  Catholics believe that God is a being within the universe.” “Which of the following did not begin at the Big Bang? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Space</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Time</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Matter</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Human beings”</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </td> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The students will be expected to </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://catholicscientists.org/scientists-of-the-past/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>research a Catholic scientist</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. They will choose a scientist and write about both their faith life and their contribution to science. The assignment will be worth 30 points.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>These are the questions that the students will have to answer by their research. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is the name of the scientist? (1 sentence) </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Give brief information about their life. (3-4 sentences). Ex. Birth, country of origin, where they went to school, etc. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Explain how the person was a faithful person. (2-3 sentences) </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain how the person was significant within the scientific community? (3-4 sentences) </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>How does the person you researched on show that there is no conflict between faith and science? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What did you enjoy the most about the person you researched? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </td> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The students will have to write a three paragraph essay answering this prompt. “Imagine that you are talking with a friend from Country Day [a local non-religious private school] about God and science. They believe that modern science, specifically the Big Bang Theory and Evolution, disprove that God exists. In a three paragraph essay, write a response to your friend about why, for Catholics understanding of God, science cannot disprove God’s existence. Your answer should touch on the following points: </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>First, that Catholics see God as existence itself, not as a being within the universe. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Second, that the Creation story is not giving us a scientific understanding of the world, but a mytho-poetic understanding of the world. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Third, that Catholics have been influential in the field of science, which shows that you can have hold scientific truths and religious truths together in harmony.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> </tr> <tr> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Jesus and the Cross</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> <td> </td> <td> </td> <td> </td> </tr> <tr> <td> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Heaven, Hell, and Purgatory</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </td> <td> </td> <td> </td> <td> </td> </tr> </tbody> </table></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><em><span>Videos : </span></em></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://youtu.be/HdPzOWlLrbE"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Video on the Big Lemaitre</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><em><span>PowerPoint Presentation: </span></em></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><a class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will know the chemical structure of plastics and the mechanism of how they endanger the environment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to identify and understand how their biases affect their decisions.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to speak to adults in ways that are conducive to a scientific and theological field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to recognize and identify some of the harmful chemicals in plastics.  This way they can avoid items that have long term harmful effects on the environment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students should be able to advocate to adults in their lives on the purchase of products that are less harmful to the environment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to discern various marketing strategies so they can make purchasing decisions that are less harmful to the environment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to identify and reduce the amount of waste they produce and understand the quantities of water that is used to produce food and other things we consume on a daily basis.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to discern between biased and misinformation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will apply elements of conscience formation in selecting environmentally responsible decisions.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><h3><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lecture - 20 minutes </span></span></span></span></span></span></h3> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>At the end of the Covalent Bond unit discuss the de</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>finition and mechanism of the formation of polymers.</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Information on plastics:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://www.compoundchem.com/2015/04/30/plastics/">https://www.compoundchem.com/2015/04/30/plastics/</a></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Student Lab Activity - Students will perform lab activity in which they determine the various types of plastics and proper disposal of each.  They will accomplish this by determining physical properties of the various types of plastics (i.e. density, transparency, luster, brittleness, rigidness and color).  They will use their results to identify an unknown and determine the best means of disposal.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <h3><span><span><span><span><span><span>Procedure for lab activity:</span></span></span></span></span></span></h3> <ul> <li><a href="https://evavarga.net/plastics-lab-activity/"><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://evavarga.net/plastics-lab-activity/</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> </ul> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><h4>Formative:</h4> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Informal assessment by walking around while students are working on the lab and asking questions to ensure that they understand the purpose of the lab and of the whole lesson. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <h4><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summative:</span></span></span></span></span></span></h4> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formal assessment will take place by grading their report containing the following sections:  Introduction, Materials, Procedure, Data, Analysis and field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate a deeper understanding of the characteristics of light in science (wave-like and particle-like) and the significance of light in theology (God is light &amp; thus its source).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Express how the fields of Science and Theology both seek Truth. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain that Science and Theology are their own fields of study, each with its limitations in its ability to understand Truth.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Defend the following statement: There is no conflict between the truths of Science and Theology.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Identify the ways in which light can be understood in both science and theology.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Identify the two ways in which Truth can be understood.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reasonably explain the relationship between the terms from the mind map (both their initial thoughts in the pre-assessment and their final thoughts in the final assessment).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Determine which questions about Truth should be answered by Science vs. which questions about Truth should be answered by Theology.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reason that Science and Theology both seek Truth and do not contradict each other in their attempt to find it.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>MULIT-LESSON Method</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Phase 1</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Introduction to Light Day</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will have a classroom discussion of the Essential Questions.  Suggestions for the discussion format are think/pair/share, google form, post-its on the board.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will watch video about light and use the simulator website (both in resources) and teacher will give a brief introduction of the wave-particle theory of light. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The teacher should watch the other video in resources prior to the lesson to help understand how to explain this concept to the students.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will then discover scripture passages or be assigned by teacher a passage (via document in resources) and explain what is it about the imagery in the selected passage that draws you to this passage. Students can finish this assignment for homework if necessary.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Phase 2: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exploration Day</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher will lead a review of the light discussion from phase 1 and solicit thoughts about the scripture passages from the students.  This discussion of scripture should begin with teacher-led thoughts of Genesis 1 as an exemplar.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will work in groups to complete the Mind Map  (Assessment #1 in resources) where they will arrange small papers with terms on them into a coherent diagram.  The teacher should cut out the terms from the google doc prior to the lesson.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Each group of students will explain the reasoning for their group’s arrangement of the terms.  Suggestions for these presentations are: projection of a picture of each group’s arrangement, have students walk around the room to view other group’s arrangements, have students pick a speaker to explain the group’s arrangement to the class.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students and teacher will engage in further discussion of relationship between science and religion.  The goal is to highlight that there is mystery in science as well as religion and that both ways of discovering Truth are valid and can coexist. Article by Chris Baglow in resources available for teacher.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will then revisit their Mind Map in light of the class discussion and make any changes to it that are appropriate.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Phase 3:  </span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summation Day</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will begin class with a review of the Mind Map and an opportunity to ask any last minute questions.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will answer the questions on the Assessment #2 as a formal assessment for this lesson.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assessment #1 - </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1ps6y-Pe4ScB5IUsdhKmPNafA0n_uaXp5wongig9V-oo/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Mind Map</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will create a MIND MAP using the following words: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>LIGHT, WAVE, PARTICLE, TRUTH, THEOLOGY, SCIENCE, THE NATURAL WORLD, DIVINE REVELATION, INTERFERENCE PATTERNS, PHOTOELECTRIC EFFECT, DISCRETE, CONTINUOUS, WHY?, HOW?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Use the arrows to <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assessment #2 - </span></span></span></span></span></span><a Truth.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How is our way of understanding light similar to our way of understanding truth?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Using the analogy of light discussed in our class, explain why/how there is no contradiction between science and theology.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson will take 2-3 class 50 minute class periods. In order to introduce the Periodic Table of Elements to chemistry students, this lesson is a history lesson on how the table was developed based on periodicity of the known elements through lecture and hands-on activity. Once students understand patterns in the Periodic Table of Elements, they will be led in reading and in discussion to articulate a Catholic understanding of God’s identity as the all-wise divine Creator of the universe.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Understand the history and development of the Periodic Table and how it relates to our understanding of the atomic model and chemical composition.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate a Catholic understanding of God’s identity as the all-wise divine Creator of the universe through comparing patterns in nature based upon patterns in the Periodic Table of the Elements.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Predict future development of the Periodic Table based on understanding of the historical development of the Table and elements known to the scientific community.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Observe patterns in nature and articulate a Catholic understanding of God’s identity as the all-wise divine Creator who put these patterns in  motion.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: *  </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read and analyze a text correlating patterns in nature as part of a divine <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduction to Mendeleev and the development of the first PTE </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Power Point <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Homework: Watch video on Mendeleev at </span></span></span></span></span></span><a <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Day 2</strong> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Mosely, Periodic Law, and the Noble Gases.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Finish Power Point presentation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read Chapter 1 Section C Intro-Subsection 1 from </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Faith, Science, and Reason: </span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span>Theology on the Cutting Edge </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(2nd edition).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Answer the following questions in written form:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>   In science we study physical laws, but this doesn’t explain where they came from. So how should we understand the origin of these laws?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>   What do these laws say about the lawgiver?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class discussion student answers to the above questions.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pose the following questions to the class and complete Think, Pair, Share activity to help students work together to answer the question.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>   From a Catholic and Christian perspective, how should we understand the relationship between Creator and creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>   Which attribute of God do natural, scientific patterns manifest and reflect? -- Wisdom</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students read John 1:1-14 for a scriptural reference during activity, if needed.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Also, have students read Chapter 1, Section D, Sub-Section 1, if needed.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students write a short paragraph to answer the last set of questions as an exit ticket. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p dir="ltr">1. Hands-on activity: By organizing known elements, students will determine the unknown elements based on the properties of the known elements and then organize all the elements using the rules of periodicity.</p> <p dir="ltr">2.  Reading and writing: Students will read an excerpt from Faith, Science, and Reason: Theology on the Cutting Edge and answer the following questions in class discussion and in writing.</p> <p>Questions:</p> <ol> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">How was Murray Gell-Mann able to accurately predict the existence of the Omega-Minus particle? How is this related to Mendeleev’s work on the development of the Periodic Table of Elements? </p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">The chemical patterns in nature point to an intelligibility in the universe at the level of atoms and molecules. In thinking about these chemical patterns through the lens of the Catholic faith, how might these patterns deepen our understanding of God as the Creator of the universe?</p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Describe other patterns that you see in nature.</p> </li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong>West Virginia Science Content Standards for Chemistry</strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>S.HS.C.1: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will use the periodic table as a model to predict the relative properties of elements based on the patterns of electrons in the outermost energy level of atoms.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>S.11-12.L.2: Students will determine the central ideas or conclusions of a text; summarize complex concepts, processes, or information presented in a text by paraphrasing them in simpler but still accurate terms.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>National Science Teacher Association Standards For High School Science</span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HS-PS-1: Matter and its Interactions. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">We intend to investigate the relationship between science and theology through the lens of Chapter 2 of Christopher’s “A Catholic’s Guide to God and the Universe”: “The Pope and the Question: Divine Creation and the Problem of Evil”. We will find places in our curricula to discuss Moral Evil in the pursuit of scientific knowledge, God’s creation of free will, and how they intersect.<br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from God</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> </span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="3"> class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Timing</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>60 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Plan Structure</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(passing time) Hook - Song of the Day - “Pave Paradise” - Counting Crows (See if the students can predict what the topic of the day will be)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(5 minutes) Introduce the reading “God creates out of freedom for the sake of freedom (Pt. 4 of the Doctrine of Creation-Chapter 1 of “In the Beginning” Chris Baglow</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(15 minutes) Read out loud and hold seminar-style discussion only on </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>first impressions</span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> following the reading from Chapter 2 on the kinds of evil from “In the Beginning” with the goal of exploring the role of scientists to freely avoid evil and bring about the good.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(5 minutes) Review list of Benedictine Values and discuss how the Values can inform scientific endeavors. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(15 minutes) Watch YouTube video on Lithium-ion battery* (13:42)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(10 minutes) Assessment: Students make an action plan, in small groups, that applies the Benedictine Values to the topic of electric vehicles.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(10 minutes) Assessment: Small groups spend 2-3 minutes presenting their analysis developed in the production of the action plan.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span> </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span> </span></span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>*This lesson is for a ninth grade physics class. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">Explore how matter and energy in the universe resulted in the formation of Hydrogen, Helium and other elements. Present scientific evidence that the Big Bang theory explains the origin of elements. God is the lawgiver who lays the framework from which the elements spring.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME Georges Lemaître, and what was he known for?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>4) What is the difference between the terms, “beginning” and “creation”?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>5) Complete the following paragraph, using these word list: Helium, Hydrogen, nuclear fusion, protons, stars and galaxies </strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>Within the first second after the Big Bang ____________ were formed.  ___________ begins within the first 3 seconds after the Big Bang, Much later  _______________  and  ________________  are formed after 300,000 years after the Big Bang,   Today we have millions of ______________  present.</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>6) Explain the process of Nucleosynthesis</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>7) Which elements were formed first?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>8) How were the heavier elements formed?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>9) What is spectrometry and how is it used in astronomy?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>10) What is the most abundant element in the Earth’s crust?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>11) What is the most abundant element in the Earth’s atmosphere?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>12) What is the most abundant element in the universe?</strong></p> <p>_____________________________________________________</p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>God, The Universe, and St. Thomas Aquinas WORKSHEET _ ANSWERS</strong></p> <p><strong>1) Name and explain the first three proofs for the existence of God,  from St. Thomas Aquinas?</strong></p> <p><strong>1.1)  Unmoved mover -- God is the “unmoved mover” who sets all of creation into motion. Students can benefit from  a video of dominoes falling to illustrate the notion of things being set into motion. https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bUl295oyeIc</strong></p> <p><strong>1.2) First cause or Uncaused cause --  God is not physical or astronomical and cannot be understood in our typical explanations of cause and effect.</strong></p> <p><strong>1.3) Necessary being -- The video narrator explains,  “God has always existed and our world finds necessity in his existence.” All being comes from God. God is the creator who “always is, was, and will be”, who created “ex nihilo” -- from nothing.</strong></p> <p><strong>2) Who was Fr. Georges Lemaître, and what was he known for?  “Fr. Georges Lemaître was a Diocesan priest from Belgium.  He is the father of the Big Bang theory.”   </strong><strong><a href="https://www.vofoundation.org/blog/priests-science-georges-lemaitre-father-big-bang/">https://www.vofoundation.org/blog/priests-science-georges-lemaitre-father-big-bang/</a></strong></p> <p><strong>“St.  John XXIII (Pope)  gave Father Lemaître the title of Prelate in the Papal Household, making him a monsignor, on March 17, 1960.”</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong><a href="https://www.catholicculture.org/culture/library/view.cfm?recnum=8847">https://www.catholicculture.org/culture/library/view.cfm?recnum=8847</a></strong></p> <p><strong>3) Which of these proofs best explains God’s creation of the universe in light of scientific evidence of the Big Bang? Give an explanation for your choice.   Answers will vary but must include an explanation which connects one of Aquinas’ arguments  with the Big Bang.</strong></p> <p><strong>4) What is the difference between the terms, “beginning” and “creation”?  LaMaitre makes a distinction between “beginning” and “creation”. When we speak of a physical or astronomical event we often use the terms “cause” and “effect”, or “beginning”. However, any discussion of “creation” and what happened “before creation” is a philosophical (specifically, metaphysical) question which transcends the senses and is outside of our physical and astronomical understandings. </strong></p> <p><strong>5) Complete the following paragraph, using these word list: Helium, Hydrogen, nuclear fusion, protons, stars and galaxies </strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>Within the first second after the Big Bang _protons_ were formed.  _Nuclear fusion_ begins within the first 3 seconds after the Big Bang,  Much later __Hydrogen__  and __Helium _ are formed after 300,000 years after the Big Bang,   Today we have millions of __ stars and galaxies_ present.</strong></p> <p><strong>6) Explain the process of Nucleosynthesis  Nucleosynthesis is a process by which the chemical elements in the universe were made through nuclear fusion</strong></p> <p><strong>7) Which elements were formed first? Hydrogen, Helium</strong></p> <p><strong>8) How were the heavier elements formed? Supernovas</strong></p> <p><strong>9) What is spectrometry and how is it used in astronomy?  </strong><strong>Spectrometry is the study of interactions between light and matter, and the reactions and measurements of radiation intensity and wavelength.  In astronomy, spectrometry is used to determine the concentration of a substance, temperature, density, and motion.</strong></p> <p><strong>10) What is the most abundant element in the Earth’s crust?  Oxygen</strong></p> <p><strong>11) What is the most abundant element in the Earth’s atmosphere?  Nitrogen</strong></p> <p><strong>12) What is the most abundant element in the universe?  Hydrogen</strong></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p dir="ltr"><strong>HS-PS2-6. Challenges A. How can we know God really exists?</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>1. Even without the Bible and Divine Revelation,we can know God really exists through reason and through experience (CCC, nos. 36-39, 50, 156-159).</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>2. By looking around at creation, reason and experience can point to God’s existence (CCC,</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>nos. 156-159).</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>a. The order and beauty of the natural world point to God as the origin and Creator of the</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>universe (CCC, no. 295).</strong></p> <p dir="ltr"><strong>b. Creation did not happen by chance; throughout history the Church has taught that someone had to be behind it, and that someone is God (CCC, nos. 156, 295).</strong></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>This is a good physics lesson which can be used to show students the scientific explanation of the formation of the first elements in the universe based on the Big Bang theory. There are many great resources (notes, videos, websites, assessments) in the lesson resource section. An important focus of the lesson is to discuss the idea of an origin versus a beginning. My only slight concern is that there are a few places in the notes where these terms seem a bit confused; however, this could be easily explained properly during the lecture. Also, it may take slightly longer than 2 days to complete the lesson, especially if you want to use all of the attached resources and give the students time to process the information.</p> </div> <!-- field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson would be situated in the context of either a general Chemistry course or an AP Chemistry course when discussing chemical bonding. The students would need a prior understanding of the general structure of atoms, the nature of chemical bonding, and angles of chemical bonds.<br /> <br /> The objective of this lesson seeks to help students to see that the order and the pattern inherent in chemical structure and bonding is reflective of the order and nature of our Creator.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>Identify examples of patterns in nature.</p> <p>Explain that the patterns of creation reflect the identify of the Creator.</p> <p>Support the explanation of the relationship between order in nature and the Creator with Scripture.</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Prior Knowledge - Chemical bonding and bonding angles (Day 0)</p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Class Discussion - Introduction to examples of patterns (Day 1)</p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Introduce Patterns in Nature Assignment (Day 1)</p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Class Discussion - Artist Analysis &amp; Nature Pictures Analysis (Day 2)</p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Think/Pair/Share - Why does this order exist?  Where does this order come from? How do you know? What evidence do you have? (from Scripture, proofs from Aquinas) (Day 3)</p> </li> <li dir="ltr"> <p dir="ltr">Assessment (Day 4)</p> </li> </ol> <p dir="ltr">A complete teacher guide is included <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1X6rTXdPPOm8Ja09qCP7U76cw3k4ECLo-1Ng2rUp0Pv0/edit?usp=drivesdk">here</a>.</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p dir="ltr">A question will be included on a unit test that assesses chemical bonding and structure.  That question is provided <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1eFheCes_9rJfjqisOltySwwDV_K5O4LDbre7n6O8RPo/edit?usp=sharing">here</a>.</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p dir="ltr"><strong>USCCB Framework</strong></p> <p dir="ltr">Course I - 2. B. God revealed in many ways. 1. Natural Revelation (CCC, nos. 32-34). a. Natural Revelation attested to in Sacred Scripture (CCC, no. 32). 1)</p> <p dir="ltr">Course I - 4. c. Scholastic theology’s arguments for the existence of God (CCC, nos. 31, 34). 1) St. Thomas Aquinas and the five proofs.</p> <p dir="ltr">Course III - 5. 2. The Trinitarian God is the Creator of all; all creation reflects the glory of God (CCC, nos. 290-295, 301).</p> <p dir="ltr">Course III - 6. 3. God created all that is, seen and unseen.  b. Seen or visible world (CCC, nos. 349-357).</p> <p><strong>Chemistry - Indiana State Standards</strong></p> <p>C.3.3 Draw structural formulas for simple molecules and determine their molecular shape.</p> <p><strong>NGSS</strong></p> <p><strong>Crosscutting Concepts -</strong> Patterns</p> <p><strong>Disciplinary Core Ideas</strong> - PS1.A: Structure and Properties of Matter</p> <p><strong>Understandings about the Nature of Science - </strong>Not all questions can be answered by science.</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from relationship of symmetry to atomic structure, electron activity, beauty, and God as the Creator of orderliness and grandeur. Students engage in reflection, class discussion, and a laboratory exercise.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>Building on prior knowledge of atomic structure and electron configuration, students will learn:</p> <ul> <li>each element has a unique electron arrangement, determined by the Aufbau Principle</li> <li>as an atom of a given element absorbs energy, electrons are excited and move to higher energy levels.  The electrons return to their original configuration, releasing a specific amount of energy, observed as a uniquely colored light and spectrum.</li> <li>natural revelation--the process by which God makes Himself known to human reason through the created world.</li> <li>to connect natural revelation, atomic structure, and color production</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span>Day 1</span></span></strong></p> <ol> <li><span><span>Students should prepare for the flame test lab by reading the protocol (found in the Lesson Files section) prior to the following activities.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Project slide or provide each student with a copy of the photographs displaying symmetry in nature (found in the Lesson Files section).</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Ask students to select one photograph that speaks to them of beauty.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>After reflecting on their choice of photograph, students discuss the reasons for their selection.  What was beautiful about the subject of the photo?</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Lead students in a discussion of symmetry as a key aspect of beauty and its origin in the laws of nature.  </span></span></li> <li><span><span>HW:  Read Christopher Baglow selection,  Chapter 7, “Twist On The Tale”  Parts E and F, from <em>Theology On The Cutting Edge</em> 2nd edition and answer the accompanying questions.</span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><strong><span><span>Day 2</span></span></strong></p> <ol> <li><span><span>Perform Flame Tests today.  This should take approximately 55 minutes to complete.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Discuss the flame tests and the questions accompanying the selection from <em>Theology On The Cutting Edge</em> that was completed for homework.  Include in your discussion, natural revelation as it relates to symmetry, beauty, and the existence of God.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Complete the Final Reflection</span></span></li> <li>HW:  Complete the Flame Test Laboratory Report if necessary</li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><h2><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>Final Reflection</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></h2> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Consider the definition for natural revelation:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong>Natural Revelation:  </strong>The process by which God makes himself known to human reason through the created world.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Choose one or more of the Scripture passages below and describe how what you learned from the flame test tells you about atomic structure and God as the “author of beauty” (C. Reissig, 2017-see link at bottom of page).*</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>And God said, “Let there be light,” and there was light. God saw that the light was good, and he separated the light from the darkness. God called the light “day,” and the darkness he called “night.” And there was evening, and there was morning—the first day. - <strong><span><span>Genesis 1:3-5</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Light is sweet, and it pleases the eyes to see the sun.  – <strong>Ecclesiastes 11:7</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Every good and perfect gift is from above, coming down from the Father of the heavenly lights, who does not change like shifting shadows. - <strong>James 1:17</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>The heavens declare the Glory of God! – <strong>Psalm 19:1</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>How great are your works, Lord, how profound are your designs! – <strong>Psalm 92:6</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>For from the greatness and the beauty of created things their original author, by analogy, is seen. – <strong>Wisdom 13:5</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><a><span><span><span><span><span>Ever since the creation of the world, his invisible attributes of eternal power and divinity have been able to be understood and perceived in what he has made.</span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span> – <strong>Romans 1:20</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>For he gave me sound knowledge of what exists, that I might know the structure of the universe and the force of its elements, The beginning and the end and the midpoint of times, the changes in the sun’s course and the variations of the seasons, Cycles of years, positions of stars, natures of living things, tempers of beasts, Powers of the winds and thoughts of human beings, uses of plants and virtues of roots—Whatever is hidden or plain I learned, for Wisdom, the artisan of all, taught me. – <strong>Wisdom 7:17-22</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span>*  <a href="https://www.crossway.org/articles/god-is-the-origin-and-author-of-beauty/">https://www.crossway.org/articles/god-is-the-origin-and-author-of-beauty/</a></span></span></span></p></div> </div> field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>NGSS  HS-PS1-1  Matter and its interactions</p> <p>NGSS  Science and Engineering Practice 3: Planning and carrying out investigations</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="flag.link_builder:build" arguments="0=node&amp;1=97&amp;2=favorite_lessons" token="1O8sTteA3rsGTWsdDmbHY1ccRL7byYpv7Jm1xTif88w"></drupal-render-placeholder> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-resources--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-resources.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-resources.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-resources field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>1). PowerPoint slide with photo collage (in Lesson Files)</p> <p>2).  Photo collage discussion prompts</p> <ul> <li>Why were you drawn to this particular photograph?</li> <li>What did you find beautiful about this photograph; the subject, the composition, or the photograph in general?</li> <li>Do you think symmetry played a role in your choice?</li> <li>Why is symmetry important in defining beauty in most cultures?</li> <li>Where do the Laws of Nature fit in this discussion?</li> </ul> <p>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</p> <p>3).  <em>Theology On The Cutting Edge</em>, 2nd edition, by Christopher Baglow excerpt with reflection questions (answer questions from Chapter 7, Section E #'s 22-28).  In Lesson Files</p> <p>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</p> <p>4).  <em>Theology On The Cutting Edge</em> Section E #'22-28 suggested answers.  </p> <p><span><span><strong><span>Suggested Answers for Theology On The Cutting Edge reflection questions 22-28</span></strong></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q22) Summarize Wisdom 13:1-5 and its message about the beauty of nature as leading to God.</span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Foolish by nature were all who were in ignorance of God, </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>and who from the good things seen did not succeed in knowing the one who is, </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>and from studying the works did not discern the artisan;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Instead either fire, or wind, or the swift air, or the circuit of the stars, </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>or the mighty water,  or the luminaries of heaven, the governors</span></span></span><span><span><span> of the world, they considered gods.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Now if out of joy in their beauty they thought them gods, </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>let them know how far more excellent is the Lord than these; </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>for the original source of beauty fashioned them.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Or if they were struck by their might and energy, </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>let them realize from these things </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>how much more powerful is the one who made them.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>For from the greatness and the beauty of created things </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>their original author, by analogy, is seen.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><em>Answer:</em></p> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>We are foolish if we do not see God as</span></span></span></em><span><span><span> <em>the artisan of all the good things we </em></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>study and observe in nature.  We should not think of the wind, water, fire, </span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>etc. as gods because there is one God who created all of nature.  The one </span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>God is more excellent and powerful than any part of nature.  By the </span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>greatness of nature we see evidence of the greatness of the original author.</span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q23) How do scientific atheists explain the phenomenon of beauty in the universe?</span></span><span><span> </span></span></p> <p><em><span><span>Answer:</span></span></em></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>Natural laws can explain the beauty and elegance we observe in nature, and no other cause is </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>needed to explain the events in the universe</span></span></em><span><span>. </span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q24) What has modern science revealed about beauty in the universe? What does this fact imply?</span></span></p> <p><em>Answer:</em></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>Modern science has discovered deeper and more complex laws that reveal even more </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>fundamental symmetry, order and beauty in the universe.  For the Christian/Catholic, </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>this more emphatically emphasizes the power of God who created all of these laws. </span></span></em></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q25) Describe the processes of discovery in science and mathematics regarding beauty in the universe.  </span></span><span><span>Why does this process reinforce that the discovery of beauty is not simply a matter of purely </span></span><span><span>personal taste?</span></span></p> <p><em>Answer:</em></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>Scientists often find a beautiful equation and then discover that it can be used to describe </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>or explain a particular phenomenon.  We know it is not a matter of personal taste </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>because the beautiful equation becomes even more ‘beautiful’ after it is found to fit </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>the phenomenon.  </span></span></em></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q26) What mistake was made in the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries by philosophers and </span></span><span><span>theologians (e.g., William Paley) regarding the Argument from Design? What did this mistake fail to </span></span><span><span>recognize?</span></span></p> <p><em>Answer:</em></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>William Paley and others claimed that the laws of nature were not able to produce all the </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>complex phenomena that we observe in nature.  They failed to recognize that since the </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>laws were created by God, they were certainly able to explain all that we observe in </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>nature, including the simple and very complex. </span></span></em></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q27) Where does the beauty that we see around us come from, according to modern physics?</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Answer: <em>                 </em></span></span></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>The creator is the originator of the universe and all of its laws.  As we discover deeper and </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>deeper truths about how the universe works, we are getting a clearer picture of the </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>magnificent order of the laws and the perfection of the mind that was their</span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span> originator.</span></span></em></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Q28) Restate the Argument from Design, using a) the notion of symmetry and b) the discovery of beauty </span></span><span><span>and order in the laws governing the universe.</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Answer: <em>                 </em></span></span></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>The beauty, harmony and symmetry that are revealed as we discover the laws governing the </span></span></em></span></span><span><span><em><span><span>universe are a sign of its creation by sublime reason.</span></span></em></span></span></p> <p><span><span><em><span><span>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</span></span></em></span></span></p> <p>5).  Flame test lab teacher pages</p> <p><span><span><strong><span>                        Flame Test Lab </span></strong></span></span><span><span><strong><span>Teacher Page</span></strong></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Materials:  wooden splints  (6-10 per group, soaked in distilled water for 24 hours; splints can be cut in </span></span><span><span>half lengthwise to conserve resources)</span></span></p> <p><span><span>                       1 beaker per group filled with distilled water</span></span></p> <p><span><span>                       1 beaker per group filled with tap water</span></span></p> <p><span><span>                       Bunsen burners</span></span></p> <p><span><span>                       Spectrometers (1 per group or 1 for each student)</span></span><span><span>(Lab can be completed without using spectrometers; students will not have the </span></span><span><span>advantage of seeing the spectral lines for each salt.  However, images of spectra can be </span></span><span><span>easily obtained on line.)</span></span></p> <p><span><span>                       Approximately 1 gram of chloride salts (possible salts: CaCl2, NaCl, SrCl2, LiCl, CuCl2, KCl)</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Teacher prep:  soak wooden splints in distilled water for 24 hours before lab.  Provide waste beakers full of tap water, into which students will put used splints.  Put a small amount (&lt; 1 gram) of metal chloride salts into small containers.  Suggested salts to use are CaCl2, NaCl, SrCl2, LiCl, CuCl2, KCl.</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Answers to questions to Think about:</span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span>Some elements display similar colors, but no two flame colors are exactly the same.  </span></span></li> <li><span><span>Only one atom of the element is needed for a successful test; since that amount is invisible, students will normally have many atoms on the splint.  As long as one atom is present, at least one electron will become excited and subsequently relax, revealing a visible colored flame.  </span></span></li> <li><span><span>When the metal is exposed to the flame, an electron will absorb a specific amount of energy, determined by the amount of energy needed for that specific electron to jump to a higher energy level.  The electron will return to its ground state and release the same amount of energy, according to the law of conservation of energy.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Each element displays a different color because it has a unique electron arrangement.  Therefore, the amount of energy absorbed when the electrons become excited is different for every element.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Potential design flaws could include contamination of samples, inability to distinguish between colors with the naked eye, students who have diminished color vision.  (Colors can be distinguished if a spectrometer is used view the flames.)</span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span>Expected colors:</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Sodium ions:  yellow</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Potassium ions: violet</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Copper (II) ions: teal</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Lithium ions: red</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Strontium ions: red</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Calcium ions: orange</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Have students prepare a lab report according to the format that is customary for the class.</span></span></p> <p>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</p> <p>6).  Flame test lab student page</p> <p><span><span><strong><span>                     Flame Test Lab </span></strong></span></span><span><span><strong><span>Student Page</span></strong></span></span></p> <p><span><span>Objective:  students will observe the unique colors that result when a metal ion is exposed to a flame and explain the origin of the colored light.</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Safety:  flame hazard:  avoid contact with flammable substances. </span></span><span><span>Safety goggles and aprons required.</span></span></p> <p><span><span>Procedure:</span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span>Prepare a data table to record the color produced by each metal chloride tested.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Light a Bunsen burner and adjust the air so a hot flame is present.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Dip a clean wet splint into the first salt so that a few grains of the salt stick to the splint.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Stick the salt coated tip of the splint into the flame; observe and record the color of the flame with your naked eye, and then look at the flame with the spectrometer.  Record the wavelength where you see a band of color and sketch the spectrum.  If colors are similar, it is important to characterize them specifically.  For example, sky blue is different from baby blue.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Dispose of the splint in the waste water beaker.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Repeat steps 3-5 for each of the metal chlorides provided.</span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span>Questions to think about:</span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span>Why is it necessary to characterize the colors specifically?</span></span></li> <li><span><span>How much of each salt is needed for a successful test?  Explain.</span></span></li> <li><span><span>What is happening when the metal is exposed to the flame, and when the colored light is visible?</span></span></li> <li><span><span>Why is the color of each metal ion unique?</span></span></li> <li><span><span>What design flaws could lead to incorrect results in this lab?</span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span>Prepare a lab report as directed by your teacher.</span></span></p> <p>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</p> <p> </p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- field--label-hidden field__item"><p>1) Emphasis on natural revelation is an excellent focus. 2) "Skills" section: Listed material seems more 'content' than 'skill' related. Reorganize this section with the "Knowledge" section. 3) Great job starting with the 'beauty discussion' and having the students identify WHY they chose the photo. Questions are open ended and relate well to the SOP. Suggestion: hang each photo in different places around the room. Give students two minutes to pick their favorite and stand by the photo. As a group, discuss why they selected it. Nominate one person from each group (nearest birthday, who ate most recently, etc) to share why the group found it beautiful. This method encourages student collaboration, physical movement, and allows opportunity for full student participation. 4) Excellent choices of Scripture; these really solidify your objective! Suggestion: Ecclesiastes and James passages are quite literal and don't pose much of a reflective challenge for the student. Remove these, but keep the others. 5) Crossway article: speaks truth to adolescents, but doesn't seem to blend well with your specific SOP. It's more about body image, makeup, weight, etc. than natural revelation found in God's non-human creation. More reading may detract from what you already have. 6) Ch. 7, Baglow: ties in perfectly and provides many more examples to support your SOP. 7) Flame Test: excellent real life application of scientific beauty. The atom complexity is sure to stir the imagination of students and the class discussion, along with reading HW questions, will help bridge the lab and theology.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from
