field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">Students will simulate the methods for the prediction of the Omega Minus particle, used by Murray Gell-Mann to win the 1969 Nobel Prize, and discover the symmetry that led the standard model of particle physics. This symmetry will also point to a Creator when considered from a theological perspective.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>TEKS 112.39 (c): <ul> <li>(5 A) describe the historical development of the concepts of gravitational, electromagnetic, weak nuclear, and strong nuclear forces</li> <li>(5H) describe evidence for and effects of the strong and weak nuclear forces in nature</li> <li>(8) Science concepts. The student knows simple examples of atomic, nuclear, and quantum phenomena.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>TEKS 112.39 (c): <ul> <li>(2J) organize and evaluate data and make inferences from data, including the use of tables, charts, and graphs</li> <li>(2K) communicate valid conclusions supported by the data through various methods such as lab reports, labeled drawings, graphic organizers, journals, summaries, oral reports, and technology-based reports</li> <li>(2L) express and manipulate relationships among physical variables quantitatively, including the use of graphs, charts, and equations.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Setup: <ul> <li>Before the students arrive, the teacher will cut out the individual particle zoo cards for each student/group. The Omega Minus particle, Eta Prime particle, and Nobel Prize cards will be removed. All other particles and cards (even the blank ones) will be given to the students.</li> <li>The students will be given the card packets, with the aforementioned cards removed, at the beginning of class. As the students inspect their card packets, background information will be lectured to the students about the particles, the state of particle physics in the early 20thcentury, and some properties they see on the cards, such as charge, spin, etc. **It is important that you do NOT reveal that there is a missing particle from the packet.**</li> <li>The Student activity sheet is optional. You could use it as a guide that you will follow orally with your students, or you can have the students fill out the entire sheet, depending on how deep you want to proceed with this lesson. I personally use the first page as an oral guide and direct questioning tool, and I use the second page as an independent or group worksheet.</li> <li>The students will be instructed to begin Part 1: finding patterns. Parts (b) and (c) require students to arrange and discover some geometric patterns in their groups. Please refer to Figure 1 on page 1 of the background information pages. The students may need some guidance to reach these patterns in some form or another, but it’s important that they reach these conclusions themselves.</li> <li>The students will eventually need to identify that there is a particle missing (Ω-, Omega Minus) and predict the characteristics of the missing particle. If the students successfully predict Omega Minus, award them the“Nobel Prize”.</li> </ul> </li> <li>Theological Perspectives: <ul> <li>In this exercise, students identify patterns and symmetry to make accurate scientific predictions about a fundamental component of nature. Symmetry in nature aided in the discovery of deeper structure within matter, just as the patterns in the periodic table led to the prediction of elements in chemistry. These patterns led to the discovery of even more fundamental particles called quarks. The ever-deepening symmetries in nature can be seen as pointing Creator.</li> <li>Important questions to ask students would be “Why is there order in nature?” “In our natural world, do you see Laws governing nature, or merely chaos?” “Why does it take years and years of study and dedication to understanding these concepts?” “What are the limitations of physics in regards to these questions?” “If we were just the result of a random series of events, why can we find beauty and symmetry in the natural world? Does is seem truly random?”</li> <li>Continue the lesson studying quark patterns with the built particle groups. Students will use the worksheet to fill out information regarding quarks.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>In congruence with the knowledge and skill of the Lesson, students will be asked to write their “NobelPrize” acceptance speech, as if they were Murray Gell-Mann. <ul> <li>In the speech, students will need to describe the historical development of weak and strong nuclear forces and quantum phenomena.</li> <li>Students will need to describe the process of the discovery of the Omega-Minus particle and its implications as if they are speaking to High School students listening to their speech.</li> <li>The speeches will be evaluated based on the inclusion and understanding of the main concepts of the lesson.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> text-formatted field field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>1) Essential questions are a great start. 4/6 are knowledge and recall; how can you make them higher-level (more analysis and application)? 2) Theological Perspective in 'Method': “If we were just the result of a random series of events, why can we find beauty and symmetry in the natural world? Does is seem truly random?” Excellent. This really drives home the point. 3) The Assessment: acceptance speech is a creative ending. Add a theological aspect, maybe tieing in a scripture passage that discusses creation, beauty, or order. A few options the students can choose from: Ecclesiastes 3:11 "He has made everything beautiful in its time. He has also set eternity in the human heart; yet no one can fathom what God has done from beginning to end.", Psalm 104:24-25 "O Lord, how manifold are your works! In wisdom have you made them all; the earth is full of your creatures. Here is the sea, great and wide, which teems with creatures innumerable living things both small and great.", Nehemiah 9:6 “You are the Lord, you alone. You have made heaven, the heaven of heavens, with all their host, the earth and all that is on it, the seas and all that is in them; and you preserve all of them; and the host of heaven worships you." Pope Paul VI, JPII, B16, or Francis quotes could work as well as various videos from scienceforseminarians.org. 4) Overall, not a strong connection between theology and science. The activity is promising, but the discussion leaves room for growth.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/contrib/bootstrap_barrio/templates/field/field--text-long.html.twig' --> field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li>In Religion classes, students will collect photos that they believe reflect the presence of God in the natural world.</li> <li>Describe why/how they believe that God’s presence is reflected in the picture.</li> <li>Students compile reflections and photos (qualitative observations) into class iBook.</li> <li>In science classes, students determine what could be quantitatively measured or qualitatively described about the objects in the reflections and photos they chose in religion classes.</li> <li>Describe the limitation and boundary of science.</li> <li>God created reality, science is an increasingly accurate but not perfect approximation of reality.</li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--comment--comment-body--comment.html.twig * field--comment--comment-body.html.twig * field--comment--comment.html.twig * field--comment-body.html.twig x field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/contrib/bootstrap_barrio/templates/field/field--text-long.html.twig' --> <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>This plan addresses the interesting question of what exactly scientific observation tells us about the natural world. However, it seems that the scientific side of the lesson focuses primarily on measurement. Since it is clear that measurements provide a necessarily limited account of reality, it seems that it might be helpful to get into some scientific "why" accounts of reality in order to more sharply indicate the limits of observational approximations. Showing the utility and limits of scientific explanatory tools would help to indicate what sort of qualitative aspects are missed. In this respect, the lesson plan's activity of reflecting upon photographs of nature and also identifying what aspects of the photos can be explained by science seems to be a useful and accessible approach.</p> <p>Finally, it would be helpful if there were more details included under the standards and resources sections.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from
